# Problem 2792

- Domain: `coding`

## Problem

```text
A 0-indexed array derived with length n is derived by computing the bitwise XOR (⊕) of adjacent values in a binary array original of length n.
Specifically, for each index i in the range [0, n - 1]:

If i = n - 1, then derived[i] = original[i] ⊕ original[0].
Otherwise, derived[i] = original[i] ⊕ original[i + 1].

Given an array derived, your task is to determine whether there exists a valid binary array original that could have formed derived.
Return true if such an array exists or false otherwise.

A binary array is an array containing only 0's and 1's

 
Example 1:

Input: derived = [1,1,0]
Output: true
Explanation: A valid original array that gives derived is [0,1,0].
derived[0] = original[0] ⊕ original[1] = 0 ⊕ 1 = 1 
derived[1] = original[1] ⊕ original[2] = 1 ⊕ 0 = 1
derived[2] = original[2] ⊕ original[0] = 0 ⊕ 0 = 0

Example 2:

Input: derived = [1,1]
Output: true
Explanation: A valid original array that gives derived is [0,1].
derived[0] = original[0] ⊕ original[1] = 1
derived[1] = original[1] ⊕ original[0] = 1

Example 3:

Input: derived = [1,0]
Output: false
Explanation: There is no valid original array that gives derived.

 
Constraints:

n == derived.length
1 <= n <= 10^5
The values in derived are either 0's or 1's
```

### Starter Code

```python
class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
```

## Generation

### System Prompt

```text
You are an expert Python programmer. You will be given a question (problem specification) and will generate a correct Python program that matches the specification and passes all tests.
```

### User Prompt

```text
### Question:
A 0-indexed array derived with length n is derived by computing the bitwise XOR (⊕) of adjacent values in a binary array original of length n.
Specifically, for each index i in the range [0, n - 1]:

If i = n - 1, then derived[i] = original[i] ⊕ original[0].
Otherwise, derived[i] = original[i] ⊕ original[i + 1].

Given an array derived, your task is to determine whether there exists a valid binary array original that could have formed derived.
Return true if such an array exists or false otherwise.

A binary array is an array containing only 0's and 1's

 
Example 1:

Input: derived = [1,1,0]
Output: true
Explanation: A valid original array that gives derived is [0,1,0].
derived[0] = original[0] ⊕ original[1] = 0 ⊕ 1 = 1 
derived[1] = original[1] ⊕ original[2] = 1 ⊕ 0 = 1
derived[2] = original[2] ⊕ original[0] = 0 ⊕ 0 = 0

Example 2:

Input: derived = [1,1]
Output: true
Explanation: A valid original array that gives derived is [0,1].
derived[0] = original[0] ⊕ original[1] = 1
derived[1] = original[1] ⊕ original[0] = 1

Example 3:

Input: derived = [1,0]
Output: false
Explanation: There is no valid original array that gives derived.

 
Constraints:

n == derived.length
1 <= n <= 10^5
The values in derived are either 0's or 1's

### Format: You will use the following starter code to write the solution to the problem and enclose your code within delimiters.
```python
class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        
```

### Answer: (use the provided format with backticks)
```

### Outputs

<details>
<summary>Generation 1</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        if n == 1:
            return True  # original[0] can be 0 (derived[0]=0) or 1 (derived[0]=0^0=0 only) -> but derived length 1 implies derived[0]=original[0]^original[0]=0
                       # However constraints allow derived[0] to be 0/1; check consistency.
        # For n>=2: construct original based on an assumed original[0]=x.
        # Let original[i+1] = original[i] ^ derived[i] for i in [0..n-2].
        # Then derived[n-1] must equal original[n-1] ^ original[0].

        # Try original[0] = 0 and 1; existence if either works.
        for x0 in (0, 1):
            orig0 = x0
            cur = orig0
            for i in range(n - 1):
                cur = cur ^ derived[i]  # cur becomes original[i+1]
            # Now cur = original[n-1]
            if (cur ^ orig0) == derived[n - 1]:
                return True
        return False
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Generation 2</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # If original is x[0..n-1], then:
        # derived[i] = x[i] xor x[(i+1) % n]
        # Compute constraints that relate all x to x0, and enforce consistency.
        x0 = 0
        cur = x0
        # After deriving x[i] relative to x0, we end up with x[n-1] and must satisfy:
        # derived[n-1] = x[n-1] xor x0  (equivalently x[n-1] must equal x0 xor derived[n-1])
        for i in range(n - 1):
            # derived[i] = cur xor x[i+1] => x[i+1] = cur xor derived[i]
            cur ^= derived[i]

        # cur is x[n-1] relative to x0; we need:
        # derived[n-1] = x[n-1] xor x0 = cur xor x0
        # Since x0=0, this becomes derived[n-1] == cur
        return derived[n - 1] == cur
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Generation 3</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # Let original[0] be x (0 or 1). Then original[i] is determined by derived.
        # original[i+1] = original[i] XOR derived[i]  (for i in [0..n-2])
        # Consistency requires: derived[n-1] == original[n-1] XOR original[0]
        
        # Try x = 0 and x = 1; if either works, return True.
        for x in (0, 1):
            first = x
            cur = x
            # Build original[1..n-1]
            for i in range(n - 1):
                cur ^= derived[i]
            # cur is original[n-1]
            last_derived = cur ^ first
            if last_derived == derived[-1]:
                return True
        return False
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Generation 4</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)

        # Let original[0] = x. Then:
        # original[i+1] = original[i] XOR derived[i]   for i in [0..n-2]
        # We only need to check consistency with the last constraint:
        # derived[n-1] = original[n-1] XOR original[0]
        #
        # After deriving all, it implies:
        # XOR(original[0], original[n-1]) == XOR(derived[0..n-1] with alternation) which simplifies to:
        # (XOR of all derived) must be 0 if n is even, else it can be anything? Actually compute:
        # original[n-1] = x XOR derived[0] XOR derived[1] ... XOR derived[n-2]
        # Need: derived[n-1] = original[n-1] XOR x
        # => derived[n-1] = (x XOR pref) XOR x = pref
        # So condition: derived[n-1] == XOR(derived[0..n-2])
        pref = 0
        for v in derived[:-1]:
            pref ^= v
        return pref == derived[-1]
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Generation 5</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        x = derived[0]  # original[0] xor original[1]
        # derived[i] = original[i] xor original[i+1] (with wrap at end)
        # Let original[0] = t. Then all original[i] are determined by t.
        # Consistency requires that the implied value for original[0] from the last equation matches t.
        
        # If original[0] = t, then:
        # original[1] = t xor derived[0]
        # original[2] = original[1] xor derived[1] = t xor derived[0] xor derived[1]
        # ...
        # Consistency from derived[n-1]: original[n-1] xor original[0] = derived[n-1]
        # which implies XOR of all derived must be 0.
        
        total = 0
        for v in derived:
            total ^= v
        return total == 0
```
```

</details>

<summary>Generation 6</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)

        # We can assume original[0] = x (0 or 1) and derive the rest uniquely:
        # original[i+1] = original[i] XOR derived[i]
        # The last constraint must satisfy:
        # derived[n-1] = original[n-1] XOR original[0]
        #
        # It turns out the derived array is valid iff:
        # XOR of all derived[i] over i equals 0 (since original[0] cancels out in the cycle).
        total = 0
        for v in derived:
            total ^= v
        return total == 0
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Generation 7</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # Let original[i] be bits. Define x = original[0].
        # For i=0..n-2: derived[i] = original[i] ^ original[i+1] => original[i+1] = original[i] ^ derived[i]
        # This determines all original[i] from x. The last constraint must also hold:
        # derived[n-1] = original[n-1] ^ original[0] = original[n-1] ^ x
        # After propagation, original[n-1] = x ^ (xor of derived[0..n-2]).
        # So derived[n-1] must equal (x ^ prefix_xor) ^ x = prefix_xor.
        prefix_xor = 0
        for i in range(n - 1):
            prefix_xor ^= derived[i]
        return prefix_xor == derived[n - 1]
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Generation 8</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # If original has length n, then:
        # derived[i] = original[i] XOR original[i+1] for i<n-1
        # derived[n-1] = original[n-1] XOR original[0]
        #
        # Let original[0] = x. Then original[i] is determined by prefix XORs of derived.
        # The only consistency condition is the last equation, which becomes:
        # original[n-1] XOR original[0] must equal derived[n-1].
        #
        # Using original[i] computed from x, this simplifies to:
        # XOR of all derived elements must be 0 for validity.
        total = 0
        for v in derived:
            total ^= v
        return total == 0
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Generation 9</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # In original array, for i<n-1: derived[i]=orig[i] xor orig[i+1]
        # So orig[i+1] = orig[i] xor derived[i]
        # Ultimately must satisfy: derived[n-1] = orig[n-1] xor orig[0]
        # Let orig[0] be x. Then orig[n-1] = x xor (derived[0] xor ... xor derived[n-2])
        # Condition becomes:
        # derived[n-1] = (x xor prefix) xor x = prefix
        # where prefix = xor of derived[0..n-2]
        prefix = 0
        for v in derived[:-1]:
            prefix ^= v
        return prefix == derived[-1]
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Generation 10</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # In binary arithmetic: if a[i] are original bits,
        # then derived[i] = a[i] xor a[(i+1) % n].
        # xor all derived: it telescopes to 0, so necessary condition:
        # xor(derived) == 0  (equivalently sum(derived) must be even)
        x = 0
        for v in derived:
            x ^= v
        return x == 0
```
```

</details>

### Prompt

```text
## Guidelines
You need to extract and summarize useful insights in the format of memory items based on comparing the successful and unsuccessful solution attempts below.
The goal of summarized memory items is to be GENERALIZABLE and TRANSFERABLE — each insight must be useful not just for this problem, but for a broad class of similar problems. Write each memory as advice that would help someone who has never seen this specific problem.

## Important notes
- You must first think about why certain attempts succeeded and others failed, then summarize the insights.
- You can extract multiple memory items from the comparison. Each should capture a distinct, independent insight.
- Prioritize GENERAL META-REASONING techniques over object-level hints. Favor principles about representation choice, constraint formalization, invariant selection, validation, decomposition, debugging, or algorithm selection.
- Convert failure observations into POSITIVE reusable guidance. Do not write memories that are just restatements of one wrong step.
- Do NOT mention specific values, answers, variable names, or problem-specific details. Every memory item must stand on its own as a general problem-solving principle or technique that transfers across different problems in the same domain.
- Avoid narrow one-off tricks unless they clearly transfer to a recurring class of problems. Fewer high-quality memories are better than many repetitive ones.
- Emphasize high-level strategies that would still make sense on a different problem in the same domain.

## Examples of good meta-reasoning memories
- Title: Constraint-First Reformulation
  Description: Turn informal requirements into explicit constraints before solving.
  Content: Rewrite vague conditions as equations, inequalities, parity rules, or state constraints. Use those formal constraints to guide the solution and reject invalid branches early.
- Title: Validate Risky Transformations
  Description: Check any step that can introduce invalid candidates against the original problem.
  Content: Squaring, dividing, relaxing constraints, or compressing state can create artifacts that look valid only in the transformed setting. Add a direct verification pass against the original conditions before committing to an answer.
- Title: Model the Smallest Faithful State
  Description: Reduce the problem to the minimal state that still determines future decisions.
  Content: If only parity, remainder class, last element, or turn matters, build the reasoning or DP around that reduced state instead of the full object. This shrinks search and makes transitions easier to verify.

### Problem
A 0-indexed array derived with length n is derived by computing the bitwise XOR (⊕) of adjacent values in a binary array original of length n.
Specifically, for each index i in the range [0, n - 1]:

If i = n - 1, then derived[i] = original[i] ⊕ original[0].
Otherwise, derived[i] = original[i] ⊕ original[i + 1].

Given an array derived, your task is to determine whether there exists a valid binary array original that could have formed derived.
Return true if such an array exists or false otherwise.

A binary array is an array containing only 0's and 1's

 
Example 1:

Input: derived = [1,1,0]
Output: true
Explanation: A valid original array that gives derived is [0,1,0].
derived[0] = original[0] ⊕ original[1] = 0 ⊕ 1 = 1 
derived[1] = original[1] ⊕ original[2] = 1 ⊕ 0 = 1
derived[2] = original[2] ⊕ original[0] = 0 ⊕ 0 = 0

Example 2:

Input: derived = [1,1]
Output: true
Explanation: A valid original array that gives derived is [0,1].
derived[0] = original[0] ⊕ original[1] = 1
derived[1] = original[1] ⊕ original[0] = 1

Example 3:

Input: derived = [1,0]
Output: false
Explanation: There is no valid original array that gives derived.

 
Constraints:

n == derived.length
1 <= n <= 10^5
The values in derived are either 0's or 1's

### Solutions
#### Correct
Attempt 1
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # If original is x[0..n-1], then:
        # derived[i] = x[i] xor x[(i+1) % n]
        # Compute constraints that relate all x to x0, and enforce consistency.
        x0 = 0
        cur = x0
        # After deriving x[i] relative to x0, we end up with x[n-1] and must satisfy:
        # derived[n-1] = x[n-1] xor x0  (equivalently x[n-1] must equal x0 xor derived[n-1])
        for i in range(n - 1):
            # derived[i] = cur xor x[i+1] => x[i+1] = cur xor derived[i]
            cur ^= derived[i]

        # cur is x[n-1] relative to x0; we need:
        # derived[n-1] = x[n-1] xor x0 = cur xor x0
        # Since x0=0, this becomes derived[n-1] == cur
        return derived[n - 1] == cur
```

Attempt 2
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # Let original[0] be x (0 or 1). Then original[i] is determined by derived.
        # original[i+1] = original[i] XOR derived[i]  (for i in [0..n-2])
        # Consistency requires: derived[n-1] == original[n-1] XOR original[0]
        
        # Try x = 0 and x = 1; if either works, return True.
        for x in (0, 1):
            first = x
            cur = x
            # Build original[1..n-1]
            for i in range(n - 1):
                cur ^= derived[i]
            # cur is original[n-1]
            last_derived = cur ^ first
            if last_derived == derived[-1]:
                return True
        return False
```

Attempt 3
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)

        # Let original[0] = x. Then:
        # original[i+1] = original[i] XOR derived[i]   for i in [0..n-2]
        # We only need to check consistency with the last constraint:
        # derived[n-1] = original[n-1] XOR original[0]
        #
        # After deriving all, it implies:
        # XOR(original[0], original[n-1]) == XOR(derived[0..n-1] with alternation) which simplifies to:
        # (XOR of all derived) must be 0 if n is even, else it can be anything? Actually compute:
        # original[n-1] = x XOR derived[0] XOR derived[1] ... XOR derived[n-2]
        # Need: derived[n-1] = original[n-1] XOR x
        # => derived[n-1] = (x XOR pref) XOR x = pref
        # So condition: derived[n-1] == XOR(derived[0..n-2])
        pref = 0
        for v in derived[:-1]:
            pref ^= v
        return pref == derived[-1]
```

Attempt 4
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        x = derived[0]  # original[0] xor original[1]
        # derived[i] = original[i] xor original[i+1] (with wrap at end)
        # Let original[0] = t. Then all original[i] are determined by t.
        # Consistency requires that the implied value for original[0] from the last equation matches t.
        
        # If original[0] = t, then:
        # original[1] = t xor derived[0]
        # original[2] = original[1] xor derived[1] = t xor derived[0] xor derived[1]
        # ...
        # Consistency from derived[n-1]: original[n-1] xor original[0] = derived[n-1]
        # which implies XOR of all derived must be 0.
        
        total = 0
        for v in derived:
            total ^= v
        return total == 0
```

Attempt 5
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)

        # We can assume original[0] = x (0 or 1) and derive the rest uniquely:
        # original[i+1] = original[i] XOR derived[i]
        # The last constraint must satisfy:
        # derived[n-1] = original[n-1] XOR original[0]
        #
        # It turns out the derived array is valid iff:
        # XOR of all derived[i] over i equals 0 (since original[0] cancels out in the cycle).
        total = 0
        for v in derived:
            total ^= v
        return total == 0
```

Attempt 6
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # Let original[i] be bits. Define x = original[0].
        # For i=0..n-2: derived[i] = original[i] ^ original[i+1] => original[i+1] = original[i] ^ derived[i]
        # This determines all original[i] from x. The last constraint must also hold:
        # derived[n-1] = original[n-1] ^ original[0] = original[n-1] ^ x
        # After propagation, original[n-1] = x ^ (xor of derived[0..n-2]).
        # So derived[n-1] must equal (x ^ prefix_xor) ^ x = prefix_xor.
        prefix_xor = 0
        for i in range(n - 1):
            prefix_xor ^= derived[i]
        return prefix_xor == derived[n - 1]
```

Attempt 7
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # If original has length n, then:
        # derived[i] = original[i] XOR original[i+1] for i<n-1
        # derived[n-1] = original[n-1] XOR original[0]
        #
        # Let original[0] = x. Then original[i] is determined by prefix XORs of derived.
        # The only consistency condition is the last equation, which becomes:
        # original[n-1] XOR original[0] must equal derived[n-1].
        #
        # Using original[i] computed from x, this simplifies to:
        # XOR of all derived elements must be 0 for validity.
        total = 0
        for v in derived:
            total ^= v
        return total == 0
```

Attempt 8
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # In original array, for i<n-1: derived[i]=orig[i] xor orig[i+1]
        # So orig[i+1] = orig[i] xor derived[i]
        # Ultimately must satisfy: derived[n-1] = orig[n-1] xor orig[0]
        # Let orig[0] be x. Then orig[n-1] = x xor (derived[0] xor ... xor derived[n-2])
        # Condition becomes:
        # derived[n-1] = (x xor prefix) xor x = prefix
        # where prefix = xor of derived[0..n-2]
        prefix = 0
        for v in derived[:-1]:
            prefix ^= v
        return prefix == derived[-1]
```

Attempt 9
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # In binary arithmetic: if a[i] are original bits,
        # then derived[i] = a[i] xor a[(i+1) % n].
        # xor all derived: it telescopes to 0, so necessary condition:
        # xor(derived) == 0  (equivalently sum(derived) must be even)
        x = 0
        for v in derived:
            x ^= v
        return x == 0
```

#### Partially Correct
Attempt 1
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        if n == 1:
            return True  # original[0] can be 0 (derived[0]=0) or 1 (derived[0]=0^0=0 only) -> but derived length 1 implies derived[0]=original[0]^original[0]=0
                       # However constraints allow derived[0] to be 0/1; check consistency.
        # For n>=2: construct original based on an assumed original[0]=x.
        # Let original[i+1] = original[i] ^ derived[i] for i in [0..n-2].
        # Then derived[n-1] must equal original[n-1] ^ original[0].

        # Try original[0] = 0 and 1; existence if either works.
        for x0 in (0, 1):
            orig0 = x0
            cur = orig0
            for i in range(n - 1):
                cur = cur ^ derived[i]  # cur becomes original[i+1]
            # Now cur = original[n-1]
            if (cur ^ orig0) == derived[n - 1]:
                return True
        return False
```

from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        if n == 1:
            return True  # original[0] can be 0 (derived[0]=0) or 1 (derived[0]=0^0=0 only) -> but derived length 1 implies derived[0]=original[0]^original[0]=0
                       # However constraints allow derived[0] to be 0/1; check consistency.
        # For n>=2: construct original based on an assumed original[0]=x.
        # Let original[i+1] = original[i] ^ derived[i] for i in [0..n-2].
        # Then derived[n-1] must equal original[n-1] ^ original[0].

        # Try original[0] = 0 and 1; existence if either works.
        for x0 in (0, 1):
            orig0 = x0
            cur = orig0
            for i in range(n - 1):
                cur = cur ^ derived[i]  # cur becomes original[i+1]
            # Now cur = original[n-1]
            if (cur ^ orig0) == derived[n - 1]:
                return True
        return False

### Parsed Memory Items

1. Seed-and-Propagate Linear Constraints
Description: When an array transform defines each output as a local XOR relation, fix one original bit and propagate to determine the rest.
<details>
<summary>Content 1</summary>

```text
For transforms that relate adjacent elements, choosing an initial “seed” value turns the system into a deterministic recurrence, letting you compute all implied original bits efficiently. After propagation, the only remaining work is to verify the final (often wrap-around or boundary) constraint to ensure the seed is consistent.
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Reasoning 1</summary>

```text
The successful approaches share a key pattern: they treat the XOR-defined derived array as linear constraints over bits, then use propagation (fixing one “seed” bit of the original) to uniquely determine the rest, and finally enforce a single wrap-around consistency condition. Several failed/partially-correct attempts stem from relying on an oversimplified global condition (e.g., total XOR equals 0) without properly accounting for how the wrap-around equation depends on the chosen seed and which derived elements are constrained. The truly correct solutions also show that different algebraic simplifications (checking last consistency vs checking prefix-vs-last vs checking total XOR) are valid only when derived constraints are handled correctly; attempts that arrived at the same condition but with incorrect reasoning or missing edge-case logic were the ones that failed.
```

</details>

2. Enforce the Unique Consistency Condition
Description: In cyclic or wrap-around constraint systems, reduce validation to checking one final equation after building the rest.
<details>
<summary>Content 2</summary>

```text
Many cyclic XOR systems become fully determined except for one global/boundary constraint. Instead of searching, derive the final implied relation between two states and check whether it matches the provided derived data; this both proves existence and avoids false positives.
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Reasoning 2</summary>

```text

```

</details>

3. Validate Global Simplifications Against the Original Equations
Description: Only accept simplified global criteria (like total XOR) if you can derive them rigorously from the exact constraints.
<details>
<summary>Content 3</summary>

```text
XOR problems often admit elegant global conditions (e.g., telescoping sums), but shortcuts can drop dependence on boundary/wrap-around terms. Use an explicit derivation or a quick verification by plugging the simplified condition back into the original boundary equation.
```

</details>

```

</details>

4. Edge Cases Need Constraint Interpretation, Not Assumptions
Description: Handle small n carefully by interpreting what the transform actually computes rather than assuming generic logic applies.
<details>
<summary>Content 4</summary>

```text
For minimal lengths, boundary/wrap-around behavior may collapse the recurrence or alter which constraints exist. Always re-check how the defining equations behave at small n to prevent inconsistencies that later algebraic steps might not cover.
```

</details>

### Baseline

### System Prompt

```text
You are an expert Python programmer. You will be given a question (problem specification) and will generate a correct Python program that matches the specification and passes all tests.
```

### User Prompt

```text
### Question:
A 0-indexed array derived with length n is derived by computing the bitwise XOR (⊕) of adjacent values in a binary array original of length n.
Specifically, for each index i in the range [0, n - 1]:

If i = n - 1, then derived[i] = original[i] ⊕ original[0].
Otherwise, derived[i] = original[i] ⊕ original[i + 1].

Given an array derived, your task is to determine whether there exists a valid binary array original that could have formed derived.
Return true if such an array exists or false otherwise.

A binary array is an array containing only 0's and 1's

 
Example 1:

Input: derived = [1,1,0]
Output: true
Explanation: A valid original array that gives derived is [0,1,0].
derived[0] = original[0] ⊕ original[1] = 0 ⊕ 1 = 1 
derived[1] = original[1] ⊕ original[2] = 1 ⊕ 0 = 1
derived[2] = original[2] ⊕ original[0] = 0 ⊕ 0 = 0

Example 2:

Input: derived = [1,1]
Output: true
Explanation: A valid original array that gives derived is [0,1].
derived[0] = original[0] ⊕ original[1] = 1
derived[1] = original[1] ⊕ original[0] = 1

Example 3:

Input: derived = [1,0]
Output: false
Explanation: There is no valid original array that gives derived.

 
Constraints:

n == derived.length
1 <= n <= 10^5
The values in derived are either 0's or 1's

### Format: You will use the following starter code to write the solution to the problem and enclose your code within delimiters.
```python
class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        
```

### Answer: (use the provided format with backticks)
```

#### Outputs

<details>
<summary>Baseline generation 1</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # Let original[0] = x. Then for i in [0..n-1]:
        # original[i+1] = original[i] XOR derived[i]  (for i < n-1)
        # and must satisfy original[0] = original[n-1] XOR derived[n-1]
        #
        # Equivalently, after propagating, we require:
        # x == x XOR (derived[0] XOR derived[1] ... XOR derived[n-1])
        # which holds iff XOR of all derived elements is 0.
        total_xor = 0
        for v in derived:
            total_xor ^= v
        return total_xor == 0
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Baseline generation 2</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # Let original[i] = x_i (binary).
        # derived[i] gives x_i XOR x_{i+1} (with x_n = x_0).
        # We can express x_i in terms of x_0:
        # x_1 = x_0 XOR derived[0]
        # x_2 = x_1 XOR derived[1] = x_0 XOR derived[0] XOR derived[1]
        # ...
        # Consistency requires:
        # x_0 XOR x_{n} where x_n = x_0 XOR (XOR of all derived[0..n-1]) to be equal to x_0
        # => XOR of all derived must be 0.
        total_xor = 0
        for v in derived:
            total_xor ^= v
        return total_xor == 0
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Baseline generation 3</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        
        # Let original[0] = x. Then for i=1..n-1:
        # original[i] = original[i-1] XOR derived[i-1]
        # Finally we need derived[n-1] == original[n-1] XOR original[0].
        
        # If we assume original[0] = 0, original[i] becomes prefix XOR of derived[0..i-1].
        # Then original[n-1] XOR original[0] equals prefix_xor_all == XOR of derived[0..n-2].
        # Condition becomes: derived[n-1] == XOR(derived[0..n-2]).
        total_prefix_xor = 0
        for i in range(n - 1):
            total_prefix_xor ^= derived[i]
        
        return total_prefix_xor == derived[n - 1]
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Baseline generation 4</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        if n == 1:
            # derived[0] = original[0] ⊕ original[0] = 0 always
            return derived[0] == 0

        # For i < n-1: derived[i] = a[i] ⊕ a[i+1]
        # So a[i+1] = a[i] ⊕ derived[i]
        # Derive all values from an assumed a[0], then check the wrap condition:
        # derived[n-1] = a[n-1] ⊕ a[0]
        # This becomes a parity constraint on XOR of derived:
        # a[n-1] = a[0] ⊕ (derived[0] ⊕ ... ⊕ derived[n-2])
        # Need: a[n-1] ⊕ a[0] == derived[n-1]
        # => derived[0] ⊕ ... ⊕ derived[n-2] == derived[n-1]
        total_xor = 0
        for x in derived[:-1]:
            total_xor ^= x
        return total_xor == derived[-1]
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Baseline generation 5</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # derived[i] = original[i] XOR original[(i+1) % n]
        # Let original[0] = x. Then original[i+1] is determined as:
        # original[i+1] = original[i] XOR derived[i]
        # Consistency requires original[n] == original[0] after wrapping.
        xor_sum = 0
        for v in derived:
            xor_sum ^= v
        # original[n] = original[0] XOR (xor of all derived)
        # Need original[n] == original[0] => xor_sum == 0
        return xor_sum == 0
```
```

</details>

```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # Let x be original[0]. Then:
        # original[1] = x ^ derived[0]
        # original[2] = original[1] ^ derived[1], etc.
        # Finally we need original[0] == original[n-1] ^ derived[n-1] (since derived[n-1]=original[n-1]^original[0])
        # This gives a parity constraint on x that must hold for both x choices; equivalently:
        # derived[0] ^ derived[1] ^ ... ^ derived[n-1] must be 0.
        xor_sum = 0
        for v in derived:
            xor_sum ^= v
        return xor_sum == 0
```
```

</details>

<summary>Baseline generation 7</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)

        # Let original[i] = x_i. Then for i < n-1: derived[i] = x_i XOR x_{i+1}
        # and derived[n-1] = x_{n-1} XOR x_0.
        #
        # If we assume x_0 = 0 or 1, the entire x_i sequence is determined.
        # We only need to check whether the implied x_{n-1} XOR x_0 equals derived[n-1].
        # But this reduces to a parity condition:
        # XOR of all derived[i] must be 0 for feasibility.
        xor_sum = 0
        for v in derived:
            xor_sum ^= v
        return xor_sum == 0
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Baseline generation 8</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        # Let original be x0..x(n-1).
        # derived[i] = x[i] xor x[(i+1)%n]
        # Choose x0 = t (0 or 1), then all x[i] are forced:
        # x1 = x0 xor derived[0], x2 = x1 xor derived[1], ...
        # Consistency requires that the computed x0 also matches the last equation:
        # derived[n-1] = x[n-1] xor x0  <=>  x[n-1] = x0 xor derived[n-1]
        # From recurrence, x[n-1] = x0 xor (xor of derived[0..n-2]).
        # Thus need: derived[n-1] == xor(derived[0..n-2]).
        # Equivalent to: xor of all derived elements must be 0.
        x = 0
        for v in derived:
            x ^= v
        return x == 0
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Baseline generation 9</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # Let original[0] = x (0 or 1). Then:
        # original[i+1] = original[i] XOR derived[i]  for i in [0..n-2]
        # and the wrap constraint must hold:
        # derived[n-1] = original[n-1] XOR original[0]
        #
        # If we propagate using original[0]=0, the resulting original[n-1] XOR original[0]
        # is determined uniquely; same for original[0]=1, but wrap check becomes equivalent
        # because XOR with original[0] cancels out. So validity depends only on parity.

        # Compute XOR of all derived elements.
        total = 0
        for v in derived:
            total ^= v

        # Condition: XOR of all derived must be 0 for consistency.
        return total == 0
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Baseline generation 10</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        
        # Let original[0] = x (0 or 1).
        # From derived[i] = original[i] xor original[i+1] (with wrap),
        # we can reconstruct all original bits as:
        # original[i+1] = original[i] xor derived[i]
        # For wrap consistency at the end we require:
        # original[0] == original[n-1] xor derived[n-1]
        #
        # This yields the condition:
        # derived[0] xor derived[1] xor ... xor derived[n-1] == 0
        total_xor = 0
        for v in derived:
            total_xor ^= v
        
        return total_xor == 0
```
```

### Augmented

### System Prompt

```text
You are an expert Python programmer. You will be given a question (problem specification) and will generate a correct Python program that matches the specification and passes all tests.
```

### User Prompt

```text
Before solving, consider these reusable insights from prior analysis:

  1. Seed-and-Propagate Linear Constraints: When an array transform defines each output as a local XOR relation, fix one original bit and propagate to determine the rest.
     For transforms that relate adjacent elements, choosing an initial “seed” value turns the system into a deterministic recurrence, letting you compute all implied original bits efficiently. After propagation, the only remaining work is to verify the final (often wrap-around or boundary) constraint to ensure the seed is consistent.
  2. Enforce the Unique Consistency Condition: In cyclic or wrap-around constraint systems, reduce validation to checking one final equation after building the rest.
     Many cyclic XOR systems become fully determined except for one global/boundary constraint. Instead of searching, derive the final implied relation between two states and check whether it matches the provided derived data; this both proves existence and avoids false positives.
  3. Validate Global Simplifications Against the Original Equations: Only accept simplified global criteria (like total XOR) if you can derive them rigorously from the exact constraints.
     XOR problems often admit elegant global conditions (e.g., telescoping sums), but shortcuts can drop dependence on boundary/wrap-around terms. Use an explicit derivation or a quick verification by plugging the simplified condition back into the original boundary equation.
  4. Edge Cases Need Constraint Interpretation, Not Assumptions: Handle small n carefully by interpreting what the transform actually computes rather than assuming generic logic applies.
     For minimal lengths, boundary/wrap-around behavior may collapse the recurrence or alter which constraints exist. Always re-check how the defining equations behave at small n to prevent inconsistencies that later algebraic steps might not cover.

Apply these insights to the problem below.

### Question:
A 0-indexed array derived with length n is derived by computing the bitwise XOR (⊕) of adjacent values in a binary array original of length n.
Specifically, for each index i in the range [0, n - 1]:

If i = n - 1, then derived[i] = original[i] ⊕ original[0].
Otherwise, derived[i] = original[i] ⊕ original[i + 1].

Given an array derived, your task is to determine whether there exists a valid binary array original that could have formed derived.
Return true if such an array exists or false otherwise.

A binary array is an array containing only 0's and 1's

 
Example 1:

Input: derived = [1,1,0]
Output: true
Explanation: A valid original array that gives derived is [0,1,0].
derived[0] = original[0] ⊕ original[1] = 0 ⊕ 1 = 1 
derived[1] = original[1] ⊕ original[2] = 1 ⊕ 0 = 1
derived[2] = original[2] ⊕ original[0] = 0 ⊕ 0 = 0

Example 2:

Input: derived = [1,1]
Output: true
Explanation: A valid original array that gives derived is [0,1].
derived[0] = original[0] ⊕ original[1] = 1
derived[1] = original[1] ⊕ original[0] = 1

Example 3:

Input: derived = [1,0]
Output: false
Explanation: There is no valid original array that gives derived.

 
Constraints:

n == derived.length
1 <= n <= 10^5
The values in derived are either 0's or 1's

### Format: You will use the following starter code to write the solution to the problem and enclose your code within delimiters.
```python
class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        
```

### Answer: (use the provided format with backticks)
```

#### Outputs

<details>
<summary>Augmented generation 1</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # Let original be x[0..n-1].
        # derived[i] = x[i] XOR x[i+1] (for i<n-1), and derived[n-1] = x[n-1] XOR x[0].
        #
        # If we pick x[0]=s, then:
        #   x[1] = s XOR derived[0]
        #   x[2] = x[1] XOR derived[1] = s XOR derived[0] XOR derived[1]
        # and in general x[k] = s XOR (derived[0] XOR ... XOR derived[k-1]).
        #
        # Final constraint for i=n-1:
        #   derived[n-1] must equal x[n-1] XOR x[0]
        #   => derived[n-1] == (s XOR prefix) XOR s == prefix,
        # where prefix = derived[0] XOR ... XOR derived[n-2].
        #
        # So requirement becomes:
        #   XOR of all derived elements must be 0.
        total = 0
        for v in derived:
            total ^= v
        return total == 0
```
```

</details>

<summary>Augmented generation 2</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # If we choose original[0] = x, then:
        # derived[0] = original[0] xor original[1]  => original[1] = original[0] xor derived[0]
        # and for i in [0..n-2]:
        # derived[i] = original[i] xor original[i+1] => original[i+1] = original[i] xor derived[i]
        # Finally we must satisfy:
        # derived[n-1] = original[n-1] xor original[0]
        #
        # We can compute the implied original[n-1] relative to original[0] by XOR-ing derived[0..n-2].
        prefix_xor = 0
        for i in range(n - 1):
            prefix_xor ^= derived[i]

        # Let original[n-1] = original[0] xor prefix_xor
        # Then requirement becomes:
        # derived[n-1] = (original[n-1] xor original[0]) = prefix_xor
        return derived[n - 1] == prefix_xor
```
```

<summary>Augmented generation 3</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)

        # We solve for original bits x[0..n-1] over XOR:
        # derived[i] = x[i] ^ x[i+1] for i=0..n-2
        # derived[n-1] = x[n-1] ^ x[0]
        #
        # Seed x[0]=0 -> propagate deterministically.
        x0 = 0
        x = [0] * n
        x[0] = x0
        for i in range(n - 1):
            x[i + 1] = x[i] ^ derived[i]

        # Check wrap-around constraint:
        # derived[n-1] must equal x[n-1] ^ x[0]
        return (x[n - 1] ^ x[0]) == derived[n - 1]
```
```

</details>

<summary>Augmented generation 4</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # Each equation gives: derived[i] = original[i] XOR original[(i+1)%n]
        # In binary/XOR terms, once we pick original[0] (seed), the rest are fixed.
        # Existence reduces to whether the wrap-around constraint is satisfied.
        
        # Try seed = 0 (seed=1 would just flip all bits; consistency check is identical)
        x = 0  # original[0]
        # Determine original[1..n-1] from original[i] = original[i-1] XOR derived[i-1]
        for i in range(1, n):
            x ^= derived[i - 1]
        # Now x equals original[n-1] given original[0]=0.
        # Wrap constraint for derived[n-1]:
        # derived[n-1] = original[n-1] XOR original[0] = original[n-1] XOR 0 = original[n-1]
        return x == derived[n - 1]
```
```

</details>

<summary>Augmented generation 5</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)

        # Let a[i] = original[i]. Then:
        # derived[i] = a[i] xor a[(i+1) mod n]
        # (because for i=n-1 it is a[n-1] xor a[0])
        # Choose a[0]=x. Then a[i] is forced:
        # a[1] = a[0] xor derived[0], ...
        # After propagating around the cycle, we just need consistency:
        # a[0] must equal a[0] implied by the last equation.

        total = 0
        for v in derived:
            total ^= v

        # The cycle consistency condition for this XOR recurrence is:
        # XOR of all derived bits must be 0.
        # - If n==1: derived[0] = a[0] xor a[0] = 0, so derived[0] must be 0.
        # - For n>1: same condition follows from chaining equations around the cycle.
        return total == 0
```
```

```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)

        # Let x[i] = original[i] in {0,1}.
        # Constraints:
        #   derived[i] = x[i] XOR x[i+1] for i=0..n-2
        #   derived[n-1] = x[n-1] XOR x[0]
        #
        # If we guess x[0], then all x[i] are forced by:
        #   x[i+1] = x[i] XOR derived[i]
        # After building x, we only need to check the wrap-around constraint.
        x0 = 0
        x = [0] * n
        x[0] = x0
        for i in range(n - 1):
            x[i + 1] = x[i] ^ derived[i]

        # Check wrap-around:
        return (x[n - 1] ^ x[0]) == derived[n - 1]
```

<summary>Augmented generation 7</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        if n == 1:
            # derived[0] = original[0] ^ original[0] = 0 always
            return derived[0] == 0

        # Let original[0] = s, then original[i+1] is determined by:
        # derived[i] = original[i] ^ original[i+1]  (for i < n-1)
        # => original[i+1] = original[i] ^ derived[i]
        # Finally we must satisfy derived[n-1] = original[n-1] ^ original[0].
        # This gives a single XOR consistency condition for s.
        # In fact, original[n-1] becomes s ^ (derived[0] ^ ... ^ derived[n-2]).
        # Then required:
        # derived[n-1] = (s ^ X) ^ s = X, where X = derived[0] ^ ... ^ derived[n-2].
        # So existence iff XOR of all derived elements equals 0.
        x = 0
        for v in derived:
            x ^= v
        return x == 0
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Augmented generation 8</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)

        # We have equations over GF(2):
        # derived[i] = original[i] XOR original[i+1] for i=0..n-2
        # derived[n-1] = original[n-1] XOR original[0]
        #
        # Let original[i] = x XOR (derived[0] XOR ... XOR derived[i-1]) for i>=1
        # where x = original[0]. Then the last equation forces x to be consistent.
        #
        # Specifically, XOR of all derived[0..n-2] gives original[0] XOR original[n-1],
        # so last equation implies:
        # original[n-1] XOR original[0] must equal derived[n-1]
        # => (original[0] XOR original[n-1]) must equal derived[n-1]
        # => XOR_all_prefix == derived[n-1]
        #
        # Compute parity of all derived[0..n-2] (equivalently total XOR of derived[0..n-1]).
        total_xor = 0
        for v in derived:
            total_xor ^= v

        # For this cyclic system, consistency is exactly total_xor == 0
        return total_xor == 0
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Augmented generation 9</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # Choose a seed for original[0] (0 or 1), propagate via:
        # derived[i] = original[i] xor original[i+1] (for i < n-1)
        # derived[n-1] = original[n-1] xor original[0]
        # This yields original[i] deterministically from the seed.
        
        def check(seed0: int) -> bool:
            orig = [0] * n
            orig[0] = seed0
            # Propagate forward using derived[i] = orig[i] xor orig[i+1]
            for i in range(n - 1):
                orig[i + 1] = orig[i] ^ derived[i]
            # Check wrap-around constraint
            return (orig[n - 1] ^ orig[0]) == derived[n - 1]
        
        return check(0) or check(1)
```
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Augmented generation 10</summary>

```text
```python
from typing import List

class Solution:
    def doesValidArrayExist(self, derived: List[int]) -> bool:
        n = len(derived)
        # Seed original[0] = x (0 or 1). Then original[i+1] is implied by:
        # derived[i] = original[i] XOR original[i+1] (with wrap for i=n-1).
        # We'll deduce original[1..n-1] from the seed and check the final wrap constraint.
        #
        # Let original[0] = x.
        # For i=0..n-2: original[i+1] = original[i] XOR derived[i]
        # Then wrap constraint for i=n-1: derived[n-1] = original[n-1] XOR original[0].
        # This reduces to: (original[n-1] XOR x) == derived[n-1], where original[n-1] computed from x.
        # It turns out the dependence on x cancels, leaving a single check:
        # XOR of all derived must be 0.
        #
        # We'll still implement via explicit propagation once to be safe/clear.

        for seed in (0, 1):
            orig0 = seed
            prev = orig0
            # compute original[1..n-1]
            for i in range(n - 1):
                nxt = prev ^ derived[i]
                prev = nxt
            # now prev == original[n-1]
            if (prev ^ orig0) == derived[n - 1]:
                return True
        return False
```
```

</details>
